      <p><b>Montenegro</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Montenegro.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0b/En-us-Montenegro.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Montenegro.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a>: <span lang="cnr"><i lang="cnr-Latn" title="Montenegrin-language text">Crna Gora</i> / <span lang="cnr-Cyrl" title="Montenegrin-language text">Црна Гора</span></span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a>&nbsp;</small>'Black Mountain', <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian">[tsr̩̂ːnaː ɡǒra]</a></span>) is a country in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">southeast Europe</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic</a> coast of the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>. It borders <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> to the southeast, the Adriatic Sea and <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> to the west. The largest and capital city <a href="/wiki/Podgorica" title="Podgorica">Podgorica</a> covers 10.4% of Montenegro's territory and is home to 29.9% of the country's population, while <a href="/wiki/Cetinje" title="Cetinje">Cetinje</a> has the status of old royal capital. Major group in the country are <a href="/wiki/Montenegrins" title="Montenegrins">Montenegrins</a>. <a href="/wiki/Serbs_of_Montenegro" title="Serbs of Montenegro">Serbs</a> form a significant minority at 28.7%, followed by <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a>. </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Early_Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Medieval">Early Medieval</a> period, three principalities were located on the territory of modern-day Montenegro: <a href="/wiki/Duklja" title="Duklja">Duklja</a>, roughly corresponding to the southern half; <a href="/wiki/Travunia" class="mw-redirect" title="Travunia">Travunia</a>, the west; and <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia_(early_medieval)" title="Principality of Serbia (early medieval)">Rascia</a> proper, the north.<sup id="cite_ref-Luscombe_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Luscombe-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sedlar_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sedlar-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Zeta_under_the_Bal%C5%A1i%C4%87i" title="Zeta under the Balšići">Principality of Zeta</a> emerged in the 14th and 15th centuries. The name Montenegro was first used to refer to the country in the late 15th century. After falling under Ottoman rule, Montenegro regained its independence in 1696 under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Petrović-Njegoš">House of Petrović-Njegoš</a>, first as a <a href="/wiki/Prince-Bishopric_of_Montenegro" title="Prince-Bishopric of Montenegro">theocracy</a> and later as a secular <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Montenegro" title="Principality of Montenegro">principality</a>. Montenegro's independence was recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Powers">Great Powers</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">Congress of Berlin</a> in 1878. In 1910, the country became a <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">kingdom</a>. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, it became part of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup of Yugoslavia</a>, the republics of <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Serbia_(1992%E2%80%932006)" title="Republic of Serbia (1992–2006)">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Montenegro_(1992%E2%80%932006)" title="Republic of Montenegro (1992–2006)">Montenegro</a> together proclaimed a <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">federation</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_independence_referendum,_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegrin independence referendum, 2006">independence referendum</a> held in May 2006, Montenegro declared its independence and the confederation peacefully dissolved.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Classified by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> as an upper middle-income country, Montenegro is a member of the UN, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Central European Free Trade Agreement">Central European Free Trade Agreement</a>. Montenegro is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Union_for_the_Mediterranean" title="Union for the Mediterranean">Union for the Mediterranean</a>. It is also in the <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Montenegro_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Montenegro to the European Union">process of joining</a> the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_city_Doclea_-_ruins_12.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Ancient_city_Doclea_-_ruins_12.jpg/220px-Ancient_city_Doclea_-_ruins_12.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Ancient_city_Doclea_-_ruins_12.jpg/330px-Ancient_city_Doclea_-_ruins_12.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Ancient_city_Doclea_-_ruins_12.jpg/440px-Ancient_city_Doclea_-_ruins_12.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5152" data-file-height="3540"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_city_Doclea_-_ruins_12.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ruins of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_settlements_in_Illyria" title="List of settlements in Illyria">ancient city</a> of <a href="/wiki/Doclea_(Illyria)" title="Doclea (Illyria)">Doclea</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country's English name derives from <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">Venetian</a> and translates as "Black Mountain", deriving from the appearance of <a href="/wiki/Lov%C4%87en" title="Lovćen">Mount Lovćen</a> when covered in dense evergreen forests.<sup id="cite_ref-visit-montenegro_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visit-montenegro-14">[14]</a></sup> In the monuments of <a href="/wiki/Kotor" title="Kotor">Kotor</a>, Montenegro was mentioned as Montenegro in 1397, as Monte Nigro in 1443 and as Crna Gora in 1435 and 1458, but there are much older papers of Latin sources where Montenegro is mentioned as Monte nigro. The first mention of Montenegro (as Monte nigro) dates to 9 November 1053 in a papal epistle and the others date to 1061, 1097, 1121, 1125, 1144, 1154, 1179 and 1189.<sup id="cite_ref-maticacrnogorska_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maticacrnogorska-15">[15]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:South-Eastern_Europe,_ca._1090,_by_User-Hxseek.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/South-Eastern_Europe%2C_ca._1090%2C_by_User-Hxseek.png/200px-South-Eastern_Europe%2C_ca._1090%2C_by_User-Hxseek.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/South-Eastern_Europe%2C_ca._1090%2C_by_User-Hxseek.png/300px-South-Eastern_Europe%2C_ca._1090%2C_by_User-Hxseek.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/South-Eastern_Europe%2C_ca._1090%2C_by_User-Hxseek.png/400px-South-Eastern_Europe%2C_ca._1090%2C_by_User-Hxseek.png 2x" data-file-width="491" data-file-height="407"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:South-Eastern_Europe,_ca._1090,_by_User-Hxseek.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Duklja" title="Duklja">Kingdom of Duklja</a> in the zenith of power, 1080 AD
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The native name <i>Crna Gora,</i> also meaning "black mountain" or "black hill", came to denote the majority of contemporary Montenegro in the 15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Fine532_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fine532-16">[16]</a></sup> Originally, it had referred to only a small strip of land under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Pa%C5%A1trovi%C4%87i" title="Paštrovići">Paštrovići</a> tribe, but the name eventually came to be used for the wider mountainous region after the <a href="/wiki/Crnojevi%C4%87_noble_family" title="Crnojević noble family">Crnojević noble family</a> took power in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Zeta" title="Upper Zeta">Upper Zeta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fine532_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fine532-16">[16]</a></sup> The aforementioned region became known as <i>Stara Crna Gora</i> '<a href="/wiki/Old_Montenegro" title="Old Montenegro">Old Montenegro</a>' by the 19th century to distinguish the independent region from the neighbouring Ottoman-occupied Montenegrin territory of <i>Brda</i> '(The) Highlands'. Montenegro further increased its size several times by the 20th century, as the result of wars against the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, which saw the annexation of <a href="/wiki/Old_Herzegovina" title="Old Herzegovina">Old Herzegovina</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/Ra%C5%A1ka_(region)" title="Raška (region)">Raška</a>. Its borders have changed little since then, losing <a href="/wiki/Metohija" title="Metohija">Metohija</a> and gaining the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Kotor" title="Bay of Kotor">Bay of Kotor</a>. </p>
      <p>After the second session of the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Fascist_Council_for_the_National_Liberation_of_Yugoslavia" title="Anti-Fascist Council for the National Liberation of Yugoslavia">AVNOJ</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_in_Yugoslavia" title="World War II in Yugoslavia">World War II in Yugoslavia</a>, the contemporary modern state of Montenegro was founded as the <i>Federal State of Montenegro</i> (<a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a>: Савезна држава Црне Горе / <i>Savezna država Crne Gore</i>) on 15 November 1943 within the Yugoslav Federation by the <a href="/wiki/State_Anti-fascist_Council_for_the_National_Liberation_of_Montenegro_and_Boka" class="mw-redirect" title="State Anti-fascist Council for the National Liberation of Montenegro and Boka">ZAVNOCGB</a>. After the war, Montenegro became a republic under its name, the <i><a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Montenegro" title="Socialist Republic of Montenegro">People's Republic of Montenegro</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a>: Народна Република Црна Гора / <i>Narodna Republika Crna Gora</i>) on 29 November 1945. In 1963, it was renamed to the <i>Socialist Republic of Montenegro</i> (<a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a>: Социјалистичка Република Црна Гора / <i>Socijalistička Republika Crna Gora</i>). As the <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup of Yugoslavia</a> occurred, the SRCG was renamed to the <i>Republic of Montenegro</i> (<a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a>: Република Црна Гора / <i>Republika Crna Gora</i>) on 27 April 1992 within the <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> by removing the adjective "socialist" from the republic's title. Since 22 October 2007, a year after its independence, the name of the country became simply known as <i>Montenegro</i>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-2" title="ISO 3166-1 alpha-2">ISO Alpha-2</a> code for Montenegro is ME and the <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-3" title="ISO 3166-1 alpha-3">Alpha-3 Code</a> is MNE.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Montenegro" title="History of Montenegro">History of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrival_of_the_Slavs">Arrival of the Slavs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Arrival of the Slavs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Duklja" title="Duklja">Duklja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Zeta" title="Principality of Zeta">Principality of Zeta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tribes_of_Montenegro" title="Tribes of Montenegro">Tribes of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A3%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BA_%D0%A6%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/%D0%A3%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BA_%D0%A6%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg/170px-%D0%A3%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BA_%D0%A6%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/%D0%A3%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BA_%D0%A6%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg/255px-%D0%A3%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BA_%D0%A6%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/%D0%A3%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BA_%D0%A6%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg/340px-%D0%A3%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BA_%D0%A6%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="785"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A3%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BA_%D0%A6%D1%80%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B0.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Uprising against the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, 1878, painted by <a href="/wiki/%C4%90ura_Jak%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Đura Jakšić">Đura Jakšić</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Three <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavic</a> principalities were located on the territory: <a href="/wiki/Duklja" title="Duklja">Duklja</a>, roughly corresponding to the southern half, <a href="/wiki/Travunia" class="mw-redirect" title="Travunia">Travunia</a>, the west, and <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia_(early_medieval)" title="Principality of Serbia (early medieval)">Raška</a>, the north.<sup id="cite_ref-Luscombe_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Luscombe-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sedlar_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sedlar-11">[11]</a></sup> Duklja gained its independence from the Byzantine Roman Empire in 1042. Over the next few decades, it expanded its territory to neighbouring Rascia and Bosnia, and also became recognised as a kingdom. Its power started declining at the beginning of the 12th century. After King Bodin's death (in 1101 or 1108), several civil wars ensued. Duklja reached its zenith under Vojislav's son, <a href="/wiki/Mihailo_I_of_Duklja" class="mw-redirect" title="Mihailo I of Duklja">Mihailo</a> (1046–81), and his grandson <a href="/wiki/Constantine_Bodin" title="Constantine Bodin">Constantine Bodin</a> (1081–1101).<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As the nobility fought for the throne, the kingdom was weakened, and by 1186, the territory of modern-day Montenegro became part of the state ruled by <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Nemanja" title="Stefan Nemanja">Stefan Nemanja</a> and was a part of various state formations ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Nemanji%C4%87_dynasty" title="Nemanjić dynasty">Nemanjić dynasty</a> for the next two centuries. After the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">Serbian Empire</a> collapsed in the second half of the 14th century, the most powerful Zetan family, the <a href="/wiki/Bal%C5%A1i%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Balšić">Balšićs</a>, became sovereigns of Zeta. </p>
      <p>By the 13th century, <i>Zeta</i> had replaced <i>Duklja</i> when referring to the realm. In the late 14th century, southern Montenegro (<a href="/wiki/Lordship_of_Zeta" class="mw-redirect" title="Lordship of Zeta">Zeta</a>) came under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Bal%C5%A1i%C4%87_noble_family" title="Balšić noble family">Balšić noble family</a>, then the <a href="/wiki/Crnojevi%C4%87_noble_family" title="Crnojević noble family">Crnojević noble family</a>, and by the 15th century, Zeta was more often referred to as <i>Crna Gora</i> (<a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">Venetian</a>: <i><i lang="vec" title="Venetian-language text">monte negro</i></i>). </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:301px;max-width:301px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Petar_I_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1_%D0%97%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8_XIX._%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Petar_I_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1_%D0%97%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8_XIX._%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0.jpg/150px-Petar_I_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1_%D0%97%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8_XIX._%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="195" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Petar_I_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1_%D0%97%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8_XIX._%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0.jpg/225px-Petar_I_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1_%D0%97%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8_XIX._%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Petar_I_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1_%D0%97%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8_XIX._%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0.jpg/300px-Petar_I_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1_%D0%97%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B8_XIX._%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="1248"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:145px;max-width:145px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Njegosh_vladika.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Njegosh_vladika.jpg/143px-Njegosh_vladika.jpg" decoding="async" width="143" height="195" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Njegosh_vladika.jpg/215px-Njegosh_vladika.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Njegosh_vladika.jpg/286px-Njegosh_vladika.jpg 2x" data-file-width="879" data-file-height="1200"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <b>Left:</b> <a href="/wiki/Petar_I_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1" title="Petar I Petrović-Njegoš">Petar I Petrović-Njegoš</a> was the most popular spiritual and military leader from the <a href="/wiki/Petrovi%C4%87_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Petrović dynasty">Petrović dynasty</a>. 
          <br><b>Right:</b> <a href="/wiki/Petar_II_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1" title="Petar II Petrović-Njegoš">Petar II Petrović-Njegoš</a> was a <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Montenegro" title="List of rulers of Montenegro">Prince-Bishop</a> (<i>vladika</i>) of Montenegro and the national poet and philosopher, Oil painting of Njegoš as vladika, c. <a href="/wiki/1837" title="1837">1837</a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1421, Zeta was annexed to the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Despotate" title="Serbian Despotate">Serbian Despotate</a>, but after 1455, another noble family from Zeta, the <a href="/wiki/Crnojevi%C4%87" class="mw-redirect" title="Crnojević">Crnojevićs</a>, became sovereign rulers of the country, making it the last free monarchy of the Balkans before it fell to the <a href="/wiki/Ottomans" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottomans">Ottomans</a> in 1496, and got annexed to the <i><a href="/wiki/Sanjak" title="Sanjak">sanjak</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Shkod%C3%ABr" title="Shkodër">Shkodër</a>. During the reign of Crnojevićs, Zeta became known under its current name&nbsp;– Montenegro. For a short time, Montenegro existed as a separate autonomous <i>sanjak</i> in 1514–1528 (<a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Montenegro" title="Sanjak of Montenegro">Sanjak of Montenegro</a>). Also, <a href="/wiki/Old_Herzegovina" title="Old Herzegovina">Old Herzegovina</a> region was part of <a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Herzegovina" title="Sanjak of Herzegovina">Sanjak of Herzegovina</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_period">Ottoman period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ottoman period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prince-Bishopric_of_Montenegro" title="Prince-Bishopric of Montenegro">Prince-Bishopric of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Large portions fell under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> from 1496 to 1878. In the 16th century, Montenegro developed a unique form of autonomy within the Ottoman Empire permitting Montenegrin clans freedom from certain restrictions. Nevertheless, the Montenegrins were disgruntled with Ottoman rule, and in the 17th century, raised numerous rebellions, which culminated in the defeat of the Ottomans in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Turkish_War" title="Great Turkish War">Great Turkish War</a> at the end of that century. </p>
      <p>Montenegro consisted of territories controlled by warlike clans. Most clans had a chieftain (<i>knez</i>), who was not permitted to assume the title unless he proved to be as worthy a leader as his predecessor. The great assembly of Montenegrin clans (<i>Zbor</i>) was held every year on 12 July in Cetinje, and any adult clansman could take part.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Vu%C4%8Dji_Do,_Orao,_1877.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Battle_of_Vu%C4%8Dji_Do%2C_Orao%2C_1877.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Vu%C4%8Dji_Do%2C_Orao%2C_1877.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Battle_of_Vu%C4%8Dji_Do%2C_Orao%2C_1877.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Vu%C4%8Dji_Do%2C_Orao%2C_1877.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Battle_of_Vu%C4%8Dji_Do%2C_Orao%2C_1877.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Vu%C4%8Dji_Do%2C_Orao%2C_1877.jpg 2x" data-file-width="784" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Vu%C4%8Dji_Do,_Orao,_1877.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vu%C4%8Dji_Do" title="Battle of Vučji Do">Battle of Vučji Do</a>, 1876
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Parts of the territory were controlled by <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Republic of Venice</a> and the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First French Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, its successors. In 1515, Montenegro became a <a href="/wiki/Theocracy" title="Theocracy">theocracy</a> led by the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitanate_of_Montenegro_and_the_Littoral" title="Metropolitanate of Montenegro and the Littoral">Metropolitanate of Montenegro and the Littoral</a>, which flourished after the <a href="/wiki/Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Petrović-Njegoš">Petrović-Njegoš</a> of Cetinje became the traditional prince-bishops (whose title was "Vladika of Montenegro"). However, the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian Republic">Venetian Republic</a> introduced governors who meddled in Montenegrin politics. The republic was succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian Empire</a> in 1797, and the governors were abolished by Prince-Bishop <a href="/wiki/Petar_II_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1" title="Petar II Petrović-Njegoš">Petar II</a> in 1832. </p>
      <p>People from Montenegro in this historical period have been described as Orthodox Serbs.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Principality_and_Kingdom_of_Montenegro">Principality and Kingdom of Montenegro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Principality and Kingdom of Montenegro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Montenegro" title="Principality of Montenegro">Principality of Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">Kingdom of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Crna_Gora_-_Oslobodjenje_od_strane_okupacije_1711-1918.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Crna_Gora_-_Oslobodjenje_od_strane_okupacije_1711-1918.png/220px-Crna_Gora_-_Oslobodjenje_od_strane_okupacije_1711-1918.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="290" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Crna_Gora_-_Oslobodjenje_od_strane_okupacije_1711-1918.png/330px-Crna_Gora_-_Oslobodjenje_od_strane_okupacije_1711-1918.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Crna_Gora_-_Oslobodjenje_od_strane_okupacije_1711-1918.png/440px-Crna_Gora_-_Oslobodjenje_od_strane_okupacije_1711-1918.png 2x" data-file-width="1903" data-file-height="2506"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Crna_Gora_-_Oslobodjenje_od_strane_okupacije_1711-1918.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Expansion of Montenegro from 1711 to 1918
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Under <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Montenegro" title="Nicholas I of Montenegro">Nicholas I</a> (ruled 1860–1918), the <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">principality</a> was enlarged several times in the Montenegro-Turkish Wars and was recognised as independent in 1878. Nicholas I established diplomatic relations with the Ottoman Empire. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Skadar_predaja_zastave.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Skadar_predaja_zastave.jpg/220px-Skadar_predaja_zastave.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Skadar_predaja_zastave.jpg/330px-Skadar_predaja_zastave.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Skadar_predaja_zastave.jpg/440px-Skadar_predaja_zastave.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="496"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Skadar_predaja_zastave.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Scutari_(1912%E2%80%931913)" title="Siege of Scutari (1912–1913)">Siege of Scutari</a>, the defeated <a href="/wiki/Ottomans" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottomans">Ottomans</a> hand over the flag to King <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Montenegro" title="Nicholas I of Montenegro">Nicholas I of Montenegro</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Minor border skirmishes excepted, diplomacy ushered in about 30 years of peace between the two states until the deposition of <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Hamid_II" title="Abdul Hamid II">Abdul Hamid II</a> in 1909.<sup id="cite_ref-ttk.gov.tr_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ttk.gov.tr-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The political skills of Abdul Hamid II and Nicholas I played a major role in the mutually amicable relations.<sup id="cite_ref-ttk.gov.tr_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ttk.gov.tr-20">[20]</a></sup> Modernization of the state followed, culminating with the draft of a Constitution in 1905. However, political rifts emerged between the reigning <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_of_Montenegro" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Party of Montenegro">People's Party</a>, who supported the process of democratization and union with Serbia, and those of the <a href="/wiki/True_People%27s_Party" title="True People's Party">True People's Party</a>, who were monarchist. </p>
      <p>In 1858 one of the major Montenegrin victories over the Ottomans occurred at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grahovac" title="Battle of Grahovac">Battle of Grahovac</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mirko_Petrovi%C4%87_Njego%C5%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Mirko Petrović Njegoš">Grand Duke Mirko Petrović</a>, elder brother of <a href="/wiki/Knjaz_Danilo" class="mw-redirect" title="Knjaz Danilo">Knjaz Danilo</a>, led an army of 7,500 and defeated the numerically superior Ottomans with 15,000 troops at <a href="/wiki/Grahovac" title="Grahovac">Grahovac</a> on 1 May 1858. This forced the <a href="/wiki/Great_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Powers">Great Powers</a> to officially demarcate the borders between Montenegro and Ottoman Empire, <i>de facto</i> recognizing Montenegro's independence. </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vu%C4%8Dji_Do" title="Battle of Vučji Do">Battle of Vučji Do</a> Montenegrins inflicted major defeat to the Ottoman Army under Grand Vizier <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Muhtar_Pasha" title="Ahmed Muhtar Pasha">Ahmed Muhtar Pasha</a>. In the aftermath of the Russian victory against the Ottoman Empire in the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_of_1877%E2%80%931878" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish War of 1877–1878">Russo-Turkish War of 1877–1878</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Great_powers_of_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Great powers of Europe">major powers</a> restructured the map of the Balkan region. The Ottoman Empire recognized independence of Montenegro in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Berlin_(1878)" title="Treaty of Berlin (1878)">Treaty of Berlin</a> in 1878. </p>
      <p>The first Montenegrin constitution (also known as the Danilo Code) was proclaimed in 1855. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kralj_i_kraljica_u_krugu_sire_familije.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Kralj_i_kraljica_u_krugu_sire_familije.jpg/220px-Kralj_i_kraljica_u_krugu_sire_familije.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Kralj_i_kraljica_u_krugu_sire_familije.jpg/330px-Kralj_i_kraljica_u_krugu_sire_familije.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Kralj_i_kraljica_u_krugu_sire_familije.jpg/440px-Kralj_i_kraljica_u_krugu_sire_familije.jpg 2x" data-file-width="928" data-file-height="638"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kralj_i_kraljica_u_krugu_sire_familije.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1_dynasty" title="Petrović-Njegoš dynasty">Royal family of Montenegro</a>: King <a href="/wiki/Nikola_I_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Nikola I Petrović-Njegoš">Nicholas I</a> with his wife, sons, daughters, grandchildren and sons- and daughters-in-law
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1910 Montenegro became <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Montenegro" title="Kingdom of Montenegro">a kingdom</a>, and as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan wars">Balkan wars</a> in 1912 and 1913 (in which the Ottomans lost most of their Balkan lands), a common border with Serbia was established, with <a href="/wiki/Shkod%C3%ABr" title="Shkodër">Shkodër</a> being awarded to a newly created <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, though the current capital city of Montenegro, Podgorica, was on the old border of Albania and Yugoslavia. Montenegro became one of the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied Powers</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> (1914–18). In the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mojkovac" title="Battle of Mojkovac">Battle of Mojkovac</a> fought in January 1916 between <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> and the Kingdom of Montenegro, Montenegrins achieved decisive victory despite being outnumbered five to one. From 1916 to October 1918 Austria-Hungary occupied Montenegro. During the occupation, King Nicholas fled the country and a government-in-exile was set up in <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux" title="Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Yugoslavia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1922, Montenegro formally became the <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Oblast" class="mw-redirect" title="Zeta Oblast">Oblast of Cetinje</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbs,_Croats_and_Slovenes" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes">Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes</a>, with the addition of the coastal areas around <a href="/wiki/Budva" title="Budva">Budva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Kotor" title="Bay of Kotor">Bay of Kotor</a>. In a further restructuring in 1929, it became a part of a larger <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Banovina" title="Zeta Banovina">Zeta Banate</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a> that reached the <a href="/wiki/Neretva" title="Neretva">Neretva</a> River. </p>
      <p>Nicholas's grandson, the Serb King <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Yugoslavia" title="Alexander I of Yugoslavia">Alexander I</a>, dominated the Yugoslav government. <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Banovina" title="Zeta Banovina">Zeta Banovina</a> was one of nine banovinas which formed the kingdom; it consisted of the present-day Montenegro and parts of Serbia, Croatia, and Bosnia. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_and_Socialist_Yugoslavia">World War II and Socialist Yugoslavia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: World War II and Socialist Yugoslavia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Italian_governorate_of_Montenegro" title="Italian governorate of Montenegro">Italian governorate of Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Montenegro" title="Socialist Republic of Montenegro">Socialist Republic of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In April 1941, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a>, and other Axis allies attacked and occupied the Kingdom of Yugoslavia. Italian forces occupied Montenegro and established it as a puppet <a href="/wiki/Italian_governorate_of_Montenegro" title="Italian governorate of Montenegro">Kingdom of Montenegro</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-185-0116-27A,_Bucht_von_Kotor_(-),_jugoslawische_Schiffe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-185-0116-27A%2C_Bucht_von_Kotor_%28-%29%2C_jugoslawische_Schiffe.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-185-0116-27A%2C_Bucht_von_Kotor_%28-%29%2C_jugoslawische_Schiffe.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-185-0116-27A%2C_Bucht_von_Kotor_%28-%29%2C_jugoslawische_Schiffe.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-185-0116-27A%2C_Bucht_von_Kotor_%28-%29%2C_jugoslawische_Schiffe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-185-0116-27A%2C_Bucht_von_Kotor_%28-%29%2C_jugoslawische_Schiffe.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-185-0116-27A%2C_Bucht_von_Kotor_%28-%29%2C_jugoslawische_Schiffe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="796" data-file-height="513"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-185-0116-27A,_Bucht_von_Kotor_(-),_jugoslawische_Schiffe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Captured ships of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Yugoslav_Navy" title="Royal Yugoslav Navy">Yugoslav Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Kotor" title="Bay of Kotor">Bay of Kotor</a> 1941.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Montenegro_(1946%E2%80%931993).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Flag_of_Montenegro_%281946%E2%80%931993%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Montenegro_%281946%E2%80%931993%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Flag_of_Montenegro_%281946%E2%80%931993%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Montenegro_%281946%E2%80%931993%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Flag_of_Montenegro_%281946%E2%80%931993%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Montenegro_%281946%E2%80%931993%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Montenegro_(1946%E2%80%931993).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Flag of the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Montenegro" title="Socialist Republic of Montenegro">Socialist Republic of Montenegro</a> within <a href="/wiki/SFR_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="SFR Yugoslavia">SFR Yugoslavia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In May, the Montenegrin branch of the Communist Party of Yugoslavia started preparations for an uprising planned for mid-July. The Communist Party and its Youth League organised 6,000 of its members into detachments prepared for <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla warfare</a>. According to some historians, the first armed uprising in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi</a>-occupied Europe happened on 13 July 1941 in Montenegro.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Unexpectedly, the uprising took hold, and by 20 July, 32,000 men and women had joined the fight. Except for the coast and major towns (Podgorica, Cetinje, Pljevlja, and Nikšić), which were besieged, Montenegro was mostly liberated. In a month of fighting, the Italian army suffered 5,000 dead, wounded, and captured. The uprising lasted until mid-August, when it was suppressed by a counter-offensive of 67,000 Italian troops brought in from Albania. Faced with new and overwhelming Italian forces, many of the fighters laid down their arms and returned home. Nevertheless, intense guerrilla fighting lasted until December. </p>
      <p>Fighters who remained under arms fractured into two groups. Most of them went on to join the Yugoslav Partisans, consisting of communists and those inclined towards active resistance; these included <a href="/wiki/Arso_Jovanovi%C4%87" title="Arso Jovanović">Arso Jovanović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sava_Kova%C4%8Devi%C4%87_(Yugoslav_Partisan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sava Kovačević (Yugoslav Partisan)">Sava Kovačević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Svetozar_Vukmanovi%C4%87-Tempo" class="mw-redirect" title="Svetozar Vukmanović-Tempo">Svetozar Vukmanović-Tempo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milovan_%C4%90ilas" title="Milovan Đilas">Milovan Đilas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peko_Dap%C4%8Devi%C4%87" title="Peko Dapčević">Peko Dapčević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vlado_Dap%C4%8Devi%C4%87" title="Vlado Dapčević">Vlado Dapčević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veljko_Vlahovi%C4%87" title="Veljko Vlahović">Veljko Vlahović</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bla%C5%BEo_Jovanovi%C4%87" title="Blažo Jovanović">Blažo Jovanović</a>. Those loyal to the <a href="/wiki/Kara%C4%91or%C4%91evi%C4%87_dynasty" title="Karađorđević dynasty">Karađorđević dynasty</a> and opposing communism went on to become <a href="/wiki/Chetniks" title="Chetniks">Chetniks</a>, and turned to collaboration with Italians against the Partisans. </p>
      <p>War broke out between Partisans and Chetniks during the first half of 1942. Pressured by Italians and Chetniks, the core of the Montenegrin Partisans went to Serbia and Bosnia, where they joined with other Yugoslav Partisans. Fighting between Partisans and Chetniks continued through the war. Chetniks with Italian backing controlled most of the country from mid-1942 to April 1943. Montenegrin Chetniks received the status of "anti-communist militia" and received weapons, ammunition, food rations, and money from Italy. Most of them were moved to <a href="/wiki/Mostar" title="Mostar">Mostar</a>, where they fought in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Neretva" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Neretva">Battle of Neretva</a> against the Partisans, but were dealt a heavy defeat. </p>
      <p>During the German operation Schwartz against the Partisans in May and June 1943, Germans disarmed large number of Chetniks without fighting, as they feared they would turn against them in case of an Allied invasion of the Balkans. After the capitulation of Italy in September 1943, Partisans managed to take hold of most of Montenegro for a brief time, but Montenegro was soon <a href="/wiki/German_occupied_territory_of_Montenegro" class="mw-redirect" title="German occupied territory of Montenegro">occupied by German forces</a>, and fierce fighting continued during late 1943 and entire 1944. Montenegro was liberated by the Partisans in December 1944. </p>
      <p>Montenegro became one of the six constituent republics of the communist <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> (SFRY). Its capital became Podgorica, renamed <a href="/wiki/Titograd" class="mw-redirect" title="Titograd">Titograd</a> in honour of President <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a>. After the war, the infrastructure of Yugoslavia was rebuilt, industrialization began, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Montenegro" title="University of Montenegro">University of Montenegro</a> was established. Greater autonomy was established until the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Montenegro" title="Socialist Republic of Montenegro">Socialist Republic of Montenegro</a> ratified a new constitution in 1974.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Montenegro_within_FR_Yugoslavia">Montenegro within FR Yugoslavia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Montenegro within FR Yugoslavia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Montenegro_(1992%E2%80%932006)" title="Republic of Montenegro (1992–2006)">Republic of Montenegro (1992–2006)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>After the dissolution of the SFRY in 1992, Montenegro remained part of a smaller <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> along with Serbia. In the <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_independence_referendum,_1992" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegrin independence referendum, 1992">referendum on remaining in Yugoslavia in 1992</a>, the turnout was 66%, with 96% of the votes cast in favour of the federation with Serbia. The referendum was <a href="/wiki/Boycott" title="Boycott">boycotted</a> by the Muslim, Albanian, and Catholic minorities, as well as the pro-independence Montenegrins. The opponents claimed that the poll was organized under anti-<a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic conditions</a> with widespread propaganda from the state-controlled media in favour of a pro-federation vote. No impartial report on the fairness of the referendum was made, as it was unmonitored, unlike in a later 2006 referendum when <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> observers were present. </p>
      <p>During the 1991–1995 <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Croatian_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Croatian War">Croatian War</a>, Montenegrin police and military forces joined Serbian troops in the attacks on <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">Dubrovnik</a>, Croatia.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> These operations, aimed at acquiring more territory, were characterized by a consistent pattern of large-scale violations of human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Montenegrin General <a href="/wiki/Pavle_Strugar" title="Pavle Strugar">Pavle Strugar</a> was convicted for his part in the bombing of Dubrovnik.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Bosnian refugees were arrested by Montenegrin police and transported to Serb camps in <a href="/wiki/Fo%C4%8Da_ethnic_cleansing" title="Foča ethnic cleansing">Foča</a>, where they were subjected to systematic torture and executed.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1996, <a href="/wiki/Milo_%C4%90ukanovi%C4%87" title="Milo Đukanović">Milo Đukanović</a>'s government severed ties between Montenegro and its partner Serbia, which was led by <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milošević">Slobodan Milošević</a>. Montenegro formed its own <a href="/wiki/Economic_policy" title="Economic policy">economic policy</a> and adopted the German <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Mark" title="Deutsche Mark">Deutsche Mark</a> as its currency and subsequently <a href="/wiki/Montenegro_and_the_euro" title="Montenegro and the euro">adopted the euro</a>, although not part of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> <a href="/wiki/Currency_union" title="Currency union">currency union</a>. Subsequent governments pursued pro-independence policies, and political tensions with Serbia simmered despite the political changes in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>. </p>
      <p>Targets in Montenegro were bombed by NATO forces during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Allied_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Allied Force">Operation Allied Force</a> in 1999, although the extent of these attacks was limited in both time and area affected.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2002, Serbia and Montenegro came to a new agreement for continued cooperation and entered into negotiations regarding the future status of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>. This resulted in the Belgrade Agreement, which saw the country's transformation into a more decentralised state union named <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a> in 2003. The Belgrade Agreement also contained a provision delaying any future referendum on the independence of Montenegro for at least three years. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_recent_history">Independence and recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Independence and recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_independence_referendum,_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegrin independence referendum, 2006">Montenegrin independence referendum, 2006</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Montenegrin_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2019–20 Montenegrin crisis">2019–20 Montenegrin crisis</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Independent_montenegro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Independent_montenegro.jpg/220px-Independent_montenegro.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Independent_montenegro.jpg/330px-Independent_montenegro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Independent_montenegro.jpg/440px-Independent_montenegro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Independent_montenegro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Supporters of Montenegrin independence in June 2006 in <a href="/wiki/Cetinje" title="Cetinje">Cetinje</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Poses_With_Montenegrin_Prime_Minister_Djukanovic,_NATO_Secretary-General_Stoltenberg,_and_Fellow_NATO_Foreign_Ministers_for_a_Family_Photo_at_NATO_Headquarters_in_Brussels_(27080758736).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Secretary_Kerry_Poses_With_Montenegrin_Prime_Minister_Djukanovic%2C_NATO_Secretary-General_Stoltenberg%2C_and_Fellow_NATO_Foreign_Ministers_for_a_Family_Photo_at_NATO_Headquarters_in_Brussels_%2827080758736%29.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Secretary_Kerry_Poses_With_Montenegrin_Prime_Minister_Djukanovic%2C_NATO_Secretary-General_Stoltenberg%2C_and_Fellow_NATO_Foreign_Ministers_for_a_Family_Photo_at_NATO_Headquarters_in_Brussels_%2827080758736%29.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Secretary_Kerry_Poses_With_Montenegrin_Prime_Minister_Djukanovic%2C_NATO_Secretary-General_Stoltenberg%2C_and_Fellow_NATO_Foreign_Ministers_for_a_Family_Photo_at_NATO_Headquarters_in_Brussels_%2827080758736%29.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4577" data-file-height="3051"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Poses_With_Montenegrin_Prime_Minister_Djukanovic,_NATO_Secretary-General_Stoltenberg,_and_Fellow_NATO_Foreign_Ministers_for_a_Family_Photo_at_NATO_Headquarters_in_Brussels_(27080758736).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Milo_%C4%90ukanovi%C4%87" title="Milo Đukanović">Milo Đukanović</a> and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Jens_Stoltenberg" title="Jens Stoltenberg">Jens Stoltenberg</a> in May 2016 with allies after signing protocol on Montenegro's accession to <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The status of the union between Montenegro and Serbia was decided by a <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_independence_referendum,_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegrin independence referendum, 2006">referendum on Montenegrin independence</a> on 21 May 2006. A total of 419,240 votes were cast, representing 86.5% of the total electorate; 230,661 votes (55.5%) were for independence and 185,002 votes (44.5%) were against.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> This narrowly surpassed the 55% threshold needed to validate the referendum under the rules set by the European Union. According to the electoral commission, the 55% threshold was passed by only 2,300 votes. Serbia, the member-states of the European Union, and the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council">permanent members of the United Nations Security Council</a> all <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_recognition" title="Diplomatic recognition">recognised</a> Montenegro's independence. </p>
      <p>The 2006 referendum was monitored by five international observer missions, headed by an <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE)/<a href="/wiki/ODIHR" class="mw-redirect" title="ODIHR">ODIHR</a> team, and around 3,000 observers in total (including domestic observers from <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Democracy_and_Technology" title="Center for Democracy and Technology">CDT</a> (OSCE PA), the Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe (PACE), the Congress of Local and Regional Authorities of the Council of Europe (CLRAE), and the European Parliament (EP) to form an International Referendum Observation Mission (IROM). The IROM—in its preliminary report—"assessed compliance of the referendum process with OSCE commitments, Council of Europe commitments, other international standards for democratic electoral processes, and domestic legislation." Furthermore, the report stated that the competitive pre-referendum environment was marked by an active and generally peaceful campaign and that "there were no reports of restrictions on fundamental civil and political rights." </p>
      <p>On 3 June 2006, the Montenegrin Parliament declared the independence of Montenegro,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> formally confirming the result of the referendum. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Law_on_the_Status_of_the_Descendants_of_the_Petrovi%C4%87_Njego%C5%A1_Dynasty" title="Law on the Status of the Descendants of the Petrović Njegoš Dynasty">Law on the Status of the Descendants of the Petrović Njegoš Dynasty</a> was passed by the Parliament of Montenegro on 12 July 2011. It rehabilitated the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Petrović-Njegoš">Royal House of Montenegro</a> and recognized limited symbolic roles within the constitutional framework of the republic. </p>
      <p>In 2015, the investigative journalists' network <a href="/wiki/Organized_Crime_and_Corruption_Reporting_Project" title="Organized Crime and Corruption Reporting Project">OCCRP</a> named Montenegro's long-time President and Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Milo_%C4%90ukanovi%C4%87" title="Milo Đukanović">Milo Đukanović</a> "Person of the Year in Organized Crime".<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The extent of Đukanović's corruption led to street demonstrations and calls for his removal.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2016, for the day of the <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_parliamentary_election,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegrin parliamentary election, 2016">parliamentary election</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegrin coup d'état attempt">coup d'état was prepared</a> by a group of persons that included leaders of the Montenegrin opposition, Serbian nationals and Russian agents; the coup was prevented.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In 2017, fourteen people, including two Russian nationals and two Montenegrin opposition leaders, <a href="/wiki/Andrija_Mandi%C4%87" title="Andrija Mandić">Andrija Mandić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milan_Kne%C5%BEevi%C4%87_(Montenegrin_politician)" title="Milan Knežević (Montenegrin politician)">Milan Knežević</a>, were indicted for their alleged roles in the coup attempt on charges such as "preparing a conspiracy against the constitutional order and the security of Montenegro" and an "attempted terrorist act."<sup id="cite_ref-rferlcoup_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rferlcoup-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Montenegro formally <a href="/wiki/Montenegro%E2%80%93NATO_relations" title="Montenegro–NATO relations">became a member</a> of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in June 2017, though "Montenegro remains deeply divided over joining NATO",<sup id="cite_ref-murkypolitico_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-murkypolitico-36">[36]</a></sup> an event that triggered a promise of retaliatory actions on the part of Russia's government.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Montenegro has been in <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Montenegro_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Montenegro to the European Union">negotiations</a> with the EU since 2012. In 2018, the earlier goal of acceding by 2022<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> was revised to 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2019_Montenegrin_anti-corruption_protests" title="2019 Montenegrin anti-corruption protests">Montenegrin anti-corruption protests</a> began in February 2019 against the incumbent President <a href="/wiki/Milo_%C4%90ukanovi%C4%87" title="Milo Đukanović">Milo Đukanović</a> and the Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1ko_Markovi%C4%87" title="Duško Marković">Duško Marković</a>-led <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Montenegro#Marković_Cabinet_(2016-present)" title="Government of Montenegro">government</a> of the ruling <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Socialists" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Party of Socialists">Democratic Party of Socialists</a> (DPS), which has been in power since 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of late December 2019, the newly adopted Law on Religion, which <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a> transfers the ownership of church buildings and estates built before 1918 from the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox Church</a> to the Montenegrin state,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> sparked a series of large<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_clerical_protests_in_Montenegro" title="2019–2020 clerical protests in Montenegro">protests</a> followed with road blockages.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Seventeen opposition <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Front_(Montenegro)" title="Democratic Front (Montenegro)">Democratic Front</a> MPs were arrested prior to the voting for disrupting the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Demonstrations continued into March<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> 2020 as peaceful protest walks, mostly organised by the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitanate_of_Montenegro_and_the_Littoral" title="Metropolitanate of Montenegro and the Littoral">Metropolitanate of Montenegro and the Littoral</a> in a number of Montenegrin municipalities.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In its political rights and civil liberties worldwide report in May 2020, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> marked Montenegro as a <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_regime" title="Hybrid regime">hybrid regime</a> rather than a democracy because of declining standards in governance, justice, elections, and media freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> For the first time in three decades, in the <a href="/wiki/2020_Montenegrin_parliamentary_election" title="2020 Montenegrin parliamentary election">2020 parliamentary election</a>, the opposition won more votes than Đukanović's ruling party.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Montenegro" title="Geography of Montenegro">Geography of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:HSV_654_07_Jan_2014_Montenegro_Holokarst.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/HSV_654_07_Jan_2014_Montenegro_Holokarst.jpg/310px-HSV_654_07_Jan_2014_Montenegro_Holokarst.jpg" decoding="async" width="310" height="363" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/HSV_654_07_Jan_2014_Montenegro_Holokarst.jpg/465px-HSV_654_07_Jan_2014_Montenegro_Holokarst.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/HSV_654_07_Jan_2014_Montenegro_Holokarst.jpg/620px-HSV_654_07_Jan_2014_Montenegro_Holokarst.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10012" data-file-height="11730"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:HSV_654_07_Jan_2014_Montenegro_Holokarst.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Satellite view of Montenegro
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Montenegro ranges from high peaks along its borders with Serbia, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, and Albania, a segment of the <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">Karst</a> of the western Balkan Peninsula, to a narrow coastal plain that is only 1.5 to 6 kilometres (1 to 4 miles) wide. The plain stops abruptly in the north, where <a href="/wiki/Mount_Lov%C4%87en" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Lovćen">Mount Lovćen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Orjen" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Orjen">Mount Orjen</a> plunge into the inlet of the Bay of Kotor. </p>
      <p>Montenegro's large karst region lies generally at elevations of 1,000 metres (3,280&nbsp;ft) above sea level; some parts, however, rise to 2,000&nbsp;m (6,560&nbsp;ft), such as <a href="/wiki/Mount_Orjen" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Orjen">Mount Orjen</a> (1,894&nbsp;m or 6,214&nbsp;ft), the highest massif among the coastal limestone ranges. The <a href="/wiki/Zeta_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Zeta River">Zeta River</a> valley, at an elevation of 500&nbsp;m (1,600&nbsp;ft), is the lowest segment. </p>
      <p>The mountains of Montenegro include some of the most rugged terrain in Europe, averaging more than 2,000 metres (6,600 feet) in elevation. One of the country's notable peaks is <a href="/wiki/Bobotov_Kuk" title="Bobotov Kuk">Bobotov Kuk</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Durmitor" title="Durmitor">Durmitor</a> mountains, which reaches a height of 2,522&nbsp;m (8,274&nbsp;ft). Owing to the hyperhumid climate on their western sides, the Montenegrin mountain ranges were among the most ice-eroded parts of the Balkan Peninsula during the last glacial period. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:R-1_regional_road_(Montenegro)_07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/R-1_regional_road_%28Montenegro%29_07.jpg/220px-R-1_regional_road_%28Montenegro%29_07.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/R-1_regional_road_%28Montenegro%29_07.jpg/330px-R-1_regional_road_%28Montenegro%29_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/R-1_regional_road_%28Montenegro%29_07.jpg/440px-R-1_regional_road_%28Montenegro%29_07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5152" data-file-height="3864"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:R-1_regional_road_(Montenegro)_07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Kotor" title="Bay of Kotor">Bay of Kotor</a>, also known locally as 'Boka Kotorska', or simply 'Boka', is designated a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> World Heritage Site.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Veliko_%C5%A0kr%C4%8Dko_jezero_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Veliko_%C5%A0kr%C4%8Dko_jezero_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Veliko_%C5%A0kr%C4%8Dko_jezero_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Veliko_%C5%A0kr%C4%8Dko_jezero_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Veliko_%C5%A0kr%C4%8Dko_jezero_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Veliko_%C5%A0kr%C4%8Dko_jezero_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Veliko_%C5%A0kr%C4%8Dko_jezero_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2248"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Veliko_%C5%A0kr%C4%8Dko_jezero_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Škrčko Lake, <a href="/wiki/Durmitor" title="Durmitor">Durmitor</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Montenegro_1_(35783841882).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Montenegro_1_%2835783841882%29.jpg/220px-Montenegro_1_%2835783841882%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Montenegro_1_%2835783841882%29.jpg/330px-Montenegro_1_%2835783841882%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Montenegro_1_%2835783841882%29.jpg/440px-Montenegro_1_%2835783841882%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Montenegro_1_(35783841882).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>National Park Skadarsko Jezero.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Internationally, Montenegro borders <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-status_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-status-56">[a]</a></sup> and Albania. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/41st_parallel_north" title="41st parallel north">41°</a> and <a href="/wiki/44th_parallel_north" title="44th parallel north">44°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/18th_meridian_east" title="18th meridian east">18°</a> and <a href="/wiki/21st_meridian_east" title="21st meridian east">21°E</a>. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Longest beach: <a href="/wiki/Velika_Pla%C5%BEa" title="Velika Plaža">Velika Plaža</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulcinj" title="Ulcinj">Ulcinj</a>&nbsp;– 13,000&nbsp;m (8.1&nbsp;mi)</li> 
       <li>Highest peak: <a href="/wiki/Zla_Kolata" title="Zla Kolata">Zla Kolata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prokletije" title="Prokletije">Prokletije</a> at 2,535&nbsp;m (8,317&nbsp;ft)</li> 
       <li>Largest lake: <a href="/wiki/Skadar_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Skadar Lake">Skadar Lake</a>&nbsp;– 391&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (151&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of surface area</li> 
       <li>Deepest canyon: <a href="/wiki/Tara_River_Canyon" title="Tara River Canyon">Tara River Canyon</a>&nbsp;– 1,300&nbsp;m (4,300&nbsp;ft)</li> 
       <li>Biggest bay: <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Kotor" title="Bay of Kotor">Bay of Kotor</a>&nbsp;– 616&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (238&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)</li> 
       <li>Deepest cave: Iron Deep 1,169&nbsp;m (3,835&nbsp;ft), exploring started in 2012, now more than 3,000&nbsp;m (9,800&nbsp;ft) long<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup></li>
      </ul>
