      <p>Montenegro is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Commission_for_the_Protection_of_the_Danube_River" title="International Commission for the Protection of the Danube River">International Commission for the Protection of the Danube River</a>, as more than 2,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (772&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of the country's territory lie within the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">catchment area</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The diversity of the geological base, landscape, climate, and soil, and the position of Montenegro on the Balkan Peninsula and Adriatic Sea, created the conditions for high biological diversity, putting Montenegro among the "hot-spots" of European and world biodiversity. The number of species per area unit index in Montenegro is 0.837, which is the highest index recorded in any European country.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Montenegro is home to three terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Balkan_mixed_forests" title="Balkan mixed forests">Balkan mixed forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dinaric_Mountains_mixed_forests" title="Dinaric Mountains mixed forests">Dinaric Mountains mixed forests</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Illyrian_deciduous_forests" title="Illyrian deciduous forests">Illyrian deciduous forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-59">[58]</a></sup> It had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 6.41/10, ranking it 73rd globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-60">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Montenegro" title="Politics of Montenegro">Politics of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:left; float:right; margin-right:9px; margin-left:2px;"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Puts_the_Cap_Back_on_His_Pen_After_Signing_an_Accession_Protocol_to_Continue_Montenegro%27s_Admission_to_NATO_in_Brussels_(27045333901)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Secretary Kerry Puts the Cap Back on His Pen After Signing an Accession Protocol to Continue Montenegro's Admission to NATO in Brussels (27045333901) (cropped).jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Secretary_Kerry_Puts_the_Cap_Back_on_His_Pen_After_Signing_an_Accession_Protocol_to_Continue_Montenegro%27s_Admission_to_NATO_in_Brussels_%2827045333901%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/120px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="170" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Secretary_Kerry_Puts_the_Cap_Back_on_His_Pen_After_Signing_an_Accession_Protocol_to_Continue_Montenegro%27s_Admission_to_NATO_in_Brussels_%2827045333901%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/180px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Secretary_Kerry_Puts_the_Cap_Back_on_His_Pen_After_Signing_an_Accession_Protocol_to_Continue_Montenegro%27s_Admission_to_NATO_in_Brussels_%2827045333901%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/240px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="631" data-file-height="895"></a></td>

        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Milo_%C4%90ukanovi%C4%87" title="Milo Đukanović">Milo Đukanović</a><br><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_Montenegro" title="President of Montenegro">President</a></small> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Zdravko_Krivokapi%C4%87" title="Zdravko Krivokapić">Zdravko Krivokapić</a><br><small><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Montenegro" title="Prime Minister of Montenegro">Prime Minister</a></small> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Montenegro" title="Constitution of Montenegro">Constitution of Montenegro</a> describes the state as a "<a href="/wiki/Civic_engagement" title="Civic engagement">civic</a>, democratic, <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">ecological</a> state of <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">reign of Law</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> Montenegro is an independent and sovereign republic that proclaimed its new constitution on 22 October 2007. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Montenegro" title="President of Montenegro">President of Montenegro</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, elected for a period of five years through direct elections. The President represents the country abroad, promulgates laws by ordinance, calls elections for the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Montenegro" title="Parliament of Montenegro">Parliament</a>, and proposes candidates for <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Montenegro" title="Prime Minister of Montenegro">Prime Minister</a>, president and justices of the Constitutional Court to the Parliament. The President also proposes the calling of a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> to Parliament, grants amnesty for criminal offences prescribed by the national law, confers decoration and awards and performs other constitutional duties and is a member of the Supreme Defence Council. The official residence of the President is in <a href="/wiki/Cetinje" title="Cetinje">Cetinje</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Montenegro" title="Government of Montenegro">Government of Montenegro</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive branch</a> of government authority of Montenegro. The government is headed by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Montenegro" title="Prime Minister of Montenegro">Prime Minister</a>, and consists of the deputy prime ministers as well as ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Montenegro" title="Parliament of Montenegro">Parliament of Montenegro</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative</a> body. It passes laws, ratifies treaties, appoints the Prime Minister, ministers, and justices of all courts, adopts the budget and performs other duties as established by the Constitution. Parliament can pass a vote of no-confidence in the Government by a simple majority. One representative is elected per 6,000 voters.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> reported that years of increasing <a href="/wiki/State_capture" title="State capture">state capture</a>, abuse of power, and strongman tactics employed by the President Đukanović have tipped his country over the edge — for the first time since 2003, Montenegro is no longer categorized as <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> and became a <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_regime" title="Hybrid regime">hybrid regime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_house_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom_house-63">[62]</a></sup> The DPS narrowly lost the <a href="/wiki/2020_Montenegrin_parliamentary_election" title="2020 Montenegrin parliamentary election">2020 Montenegrin parliamentary election</a>, ending its 30-year rule.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_of_Montenegro">Foreign relations of Montenegro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Foreign relations of Montenegro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Montenegro" title="Foreign relations of Montenegro">Foreign relations of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_a_Press_Availability_in_Montenegro_(48844398567).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_a_Press_Availability_in_Montenegro_%2848844398567%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_a_Press_Availability_in_Montenegro_%2848844398567%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_a_Press_Availability_in_Montenegro_%2848844398567%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_a_Press_Availability_in_Montenegro_%2848844398567%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_a_Press_Availability_in_Montenegro_%2848844398567%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_a_Press_Availability_in_Montenegro_%2848844398567%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5263" data-file-height="3509"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_Participates_in_a_Press_Availability_in_Montenegro_(48844398567).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Du%C5%A1ko_Markovi%C4%87" title="Duško Marković">Duško Marković</a> and U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Mike_Pompeo" title="Mike Pompeo">Mike Pompeo</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the promulgation of the Declaration of Independence in the Parliament of the Republic of Montenegro on 3 June 2006, following the independence referendum held on 21 May, the Government of the Republic of Montenegro assumed the competences of defining and conducting the foreign policy of Montenegro as a subject of international law and a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a>. The implementation of this constitutional responsibility was vested in the Ministry of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Affairs" title="Foreign Affairs">Foreign Affairs</a>, which was given the task of defining the foreign policy priorities and activities needed for their implementation. These activities are pursued in close cooperation with other state administration authorities, the President, the Speaker of the Parliament, and other relevant stakeholders.<sup id="cite_ref-mvpei.gov.me_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mvpei.gov.me-65">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Integration into the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> is Montenegro's strategic goal. This process will remain in the focus of Montenegrin foreign policy in the short term. The second strategic and equally important goal, but one attainable in a shorter time span, was joining <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, which would guarantee stability and security for pursuing other strategic goals. Montenegro believes NATO integration would speed up EU integration.<sup id="cite_ref-mvpei.gov.me_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mvpei.gov.me-65">[64]</a></sup> In May 2017 NATO accepted Montenegro as a NATO member starting 5 June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/National_symbols_of_Montenegro" title="National symbols of Montenegro">National symbols of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Njegos_mausoleum_montenegro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Njegos_mausoleum_montenegro.jpg/220px-Njegos_mausoleum_montenegro.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Njegos_mausoleum_montenegro.jpg/330px-Njegos_mausoleum_montenegro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Njegos_mausoleum_montenegro.jpg/440px-Njegos_mausoleum_montenegro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1680" data-file-height="1120"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Njegos_mausoleum_montenegro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mausoleum_of_Njego%C5%A1" title="Mausoleum of Njegoš">Mausoleum</a> of <a href="/wiki/Petar_II_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1" title="Petar II Petrović-Njegoš">Petar II Petrović-Njegoš</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Lov%C4%87en" title="Lovćen">Lovćen</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>An official <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Montenegro" title="Flag of Montenegro">flag of Montenegro</a>, based on the royal standard of <a href="/wiki/King_Nicholas_I" class="mw-redirect" title="King Nicholas I">King Nicholas I</a>, was adopted on 12 July 2004 by the Montenegrin legislature. This royal flag was red with a silver border, a silver coat of arms, and the initials НІ, in Cyrillic script (corresponding to NI in Latin script), representing King Nicholas I.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On the current flag, the border and arms are in gold and the royal cipher in the centre of the arms has been replaced with a golden lion. </p>
      <p>The national day of <a href="/wiki/Statehood_Day_(Montenegro)" title="Statehood Day (Montenegro)">13 July</a> marks the date in 1878 when the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">Congress of Berlin</a> recognized Montenegro as the 27th independent state in the world<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> and the start of one of the first popular uprisings in Europe against the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis Powers</a> on 13 July 1941 in Montenegro. </p>
      <p>In 2004, the Montenegrin legislature selected a popular Montenegrin traditional song, "<a href="/wiki/Oj,_svijetla_majska_zoro" title="Oj, svijetla majska zoro">Oh, Bright Dawn of May</a>", as the <a href="/wiki/National_anthem" title="National anthem">national anthem</a>. Montenegro's official anthem during the reign of King Nicholas I was <i><a href="/wiki/Ubavoj_nam_Crnoj_Gori" title="Ubavoj nam Crnoj Gori">Ubavoj nam Crnoj Gori</a></i> ("To Our Beautiful Montenegro"). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Montenegro" title="Armed Forces of Montenegro">Armed Forces of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Military_Montenegro_11.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Military_Montenegro_11.jpg/220px-Military_Montenegro_11.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Military_Montenegro_11.jpg/330px-Military_Montenegro_11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Military_Montenegro_11.jpg/440px-Military_Montenegro_11.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Military_Montenegro_11.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Montenegro" title="Armed Forces of Montenegro">Armed Forces of Montenegro</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Patrolni_brod_klasa_Kotor_P34.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Patrolni_brod_klasa_Kotor_P34.jpg/220px-Patrolni_brod_klasa_Kotor_P34.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Patrolni_brod_klasa_Kotor_P34.jpg/330px-Patrolni_brod_klasa_Kotor_P34.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Patrolni_brod_klasa_Kotor_P34.jpg/440px-Patrolni_brod_klasa_Kotor_P34.jpg 2x" data-file-width="699" data-file-height="435"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Patrolni_brod_klasa_Kotor_P34.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kotor-class_frigate" title="Kotor-class frigate">Kotor-class frigate</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Montenegro" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Montenegro">military of Montenegro</a> is a fully professional <a href="/wiki/Standing_army" title="Standing army">standing army</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Montenegro)" title="Ministry of Defence (Montenegro)">Ministry of Defence</a> and is composed of the <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_Ground_Army" title="Montenegrin Ground Army">Montenegrin Ground Army</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_Navy" title="Montenegrin Navy">Montenegrin Navy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_Air_Force" title="Montenegrin Air Force">Montenegrin Air Force</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Special_forces" title="Special forces">special forces</a>. Conscription was abolished in 2006. The military currently maintains a force of 1,920 active duty members. The bulk of its equipment and forces were inherited from the armed forces of the State Union of <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a>; as Montenegro contained the entire <a href="/wiki/Coastline" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastline">coastline</a> of the former union, it retained practically the entire naval force. </p>
      <p>Montenegro was a member of NATO's <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> program and then became an official candidate for full membership in the alliance. Montenegro applied for a <a href="/wiki/Membership_Action_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Membership Action Plan">Membership Action Plan</a> on 5 November 2008, which was granted in December 2009. Montenegro is also a member of <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Charter" title="Adriatic Charter">Adriatic Charter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> Montenegro was invited to join <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> on 2 December 2015 and on 19 May 2016, NATO and Montenegro conducted a signing ceremony at NATO headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> for Montenegro's membership invitation.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> Montenegro became NATO's 29th <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_NATO" title="Member states of NATO">member</a> on 5 June 2017, despite Russia's objections.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> The government plans to have the army participate in <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> missions through the UN and NATO such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force" title="International Security Assistance Force">International Security Assistance Force</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Montenegro" title="Municipalities of Montenegro">Municipalities of Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Montenegro" class="mw-redirect" title="List of regions of Montenegro">List of regions of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Montenegro is divided into twenty-three municipalities (<i><a href="/wiki/Op%C5%A1tina" title="Opština">opština</a></i>). This includes 21 District-level Municipalities and 2 Urban Municipalities, with two subdivisions of <a href="/wiki/Municipality_of_Podgorica" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipality of Podgorica">Podgorica municipality</a>, listed below. Each municipality can contain multiple cities and towns. Historically, the territory of the country was divided into "nahije". </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Montenegro,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Montenegro%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/220px-Montenegro%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Montenegro%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/330px-Montenegro%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Montenegro%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/440px-Montenegro%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1063" data-file-height="1285"></a>

          <a href="/wiki/File:Montenegro,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Municipalities of Montenegro.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Montenegro" title="Economy of Montenegro">Economy of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Euro_coins_and_banknotes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Euro_coins_and_banknotes.jpg/220px-Euro_coins_and_banknotes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Euro_coins_and_banknotes.jpg/330px-Euro_coins_and_banknotes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Euro_coins_and_banknotes.jpg/440px-Euro_coins_and_banknotes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Euro_coins_and_banknotes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The official currency of Montenegro is the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The economy of Montenegro is mostly <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">service-based</a> and is in <a href="/wiki/Transition_economy" title="Transition economy">late transition</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">nominal GDP</a> of Montenegro was $5.424&nbsp;billion in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-WEO2019_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WEO2019-7">[7]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">GDP PPP</a> for 2019 was $12.516&nbsp;billion, or $20,083 per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-WEO2019_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WEO2019-7">[7]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> data, the Montenegrin GDP per capita stood at 48% of the EU average in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Montenegro" title="Central Bank of Montenegro">Central Bank of Montenegro</a> is not part of the euro system but the country is "<a href="/wiki/Euroisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Euroisation">euroised</a>", using <a href="/wiki/Montenegro_and_the_euro" title="Montenegro and the euro">the euro unilaterally</a> as its currency. </p>
      <p>GDP grew at 10.7% in 2007 and 7.5% in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> The country entered a <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">recession</a> in 2008 as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Late-2000s_recession" class="mw-redirect" title="Late-2000s recession">global recession</a>, with GDP contracting by 4%. However, Montenegro remained a target for <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign investment</a>, the only country in the Balkans to increase its amount of direct foreign investment.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> The country exited the recession in mid-2010, with GDP growth at around 0.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> However, the significant dependence of the Montenegrin economy on <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> leaves it susceptible to external shocks and a high export/import trade deficit. </p>
      <p>In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Service_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Service sector">service sector</a> made up 72.4% of GDP, with industry and agriculture making up the rest at 17.6% and 10%, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-WB_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB-77">[76]</a></sup> There are 50,000 farming households in Montenegro that rely on agriculture to fill the family budget.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Montenegro_motorways.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Montenegro_motorways.JPG/180px-Montenegro_motorways.JPG" decoding="async" width="180" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Montenegro_motorways.JPG/270px-Montenegro_motorways.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Montenegro_motorways.JPG/360px-Montenegro_motorways.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1453" data-file-height="1953"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Montenegro_motorways.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Roads of Montenegro in service and two planned: red – <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Bar_motorway" title="Belgrade–Bar motorway">Bar–Boljare highway</a>, blue – <a href="/wiki/Adriatic%E2%80%93Ionian_motorway" title="Adriatic–Ionian motorway">Adriatic–Ionian motorway</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Montenegro" title="Transport in Montenegro">Transport in Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Brueckenbau_Montenegro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Brueckenbau_Montenegro.jpg/220px-Brueckenbau_Montenegro.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Brueckenbau_Montenegro.jpg/330px-Brueckenbau_Montenegro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Brueckenbau_Montenegro.jpg/440px-Brueckenbau_Montenegro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5847" data-file-height="3899"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Brueckenbau_Montenegro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Moračica Bridge is the highest bridge in the Western Balkans and it is the part of the future Bar-Boljare highway, September 2019
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Montenegrin road infrastructure is not yet at Western European standards. Despite an extensive road network, no roads are built to full motorway standards. Construction of new motorways is considered a national priority, as they are important for uniform regional economic development and the development of Montenegro as an attractive tourist destination. </p>
      <p>Current <a href="/wiki/European_route" class="mw-redirect" title="European route">European routes</a> that pass through Montenegro are <a href="/wiki/European_route_E65" title="European route E65">E65</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_route_E80" title="European route E80">E80</a>. </p>
      <p>The backbone of the Montenegrin rail network is the <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Bar_railway" title="Belgrade–Bar railway">Belgrade–Bar railway</a>, which provides international connection towards <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>. There is a domestic branch line, the <a href="/wiki/Nik%C5%A1i%C4%87-Podgorica_railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Nikšić-Podgorica railway">Nikšić-Podgorica railway</a>, which was operated as a freight-only line for decades, and is now also open for passenger traffic after the reconstruction and electrification works in 2012. The other branch line from Podgorica towards the Albanian border, the <a href="/wiki/Podgorica%E2%80%93Shkod%C3%ABr_railway" title="Podgorica–Shkodër railway">Podgorica–Shkodër railway</a>, is not in use. </p>
      <p>Montenegro has two international airports, <a href="/wiki/Podgorica_Airport" title="Podgorica Airport">Podgorica Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tivat_Airport" title="Tivat Airport">Tivat Airport</a>. The two airports served 1.1&nbsp;million passengers in 2008. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Bar" title="Port of Bar">Port of Bar</a> is Montenegro's main seaport. Initially built in 1906, the port was almost completely destroyed during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, with reconstruction beginning in 1950. Today, it is equipped to handle over 5 million tons of cargo annually, though the breakup of the former Yugoslavia and the size of the Montenegrin industrial sector has resulted in the port operating at a loss and well below capacity for several years. The reconstruction of the <a href="/wiki/Belgrade-Bar_railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgrade-Bar railway">Belgrade-Bar railway</a> and the proposed <a href="/wiki/Belgrade-Bar_motorway" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgrade-Bar motorway">Belgrade-Bar motorway</a> are expected to bring the port back up to capacity. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Montenegro" title="Tourism in Montenegro">Tourism in Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Widok_na_Perast_z_zachodu_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Widok_na_Perast_z_zachodu_01.JPG/220px-Widok_na_Perast_z_zachodu_01.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Widok_na_Perast_z_zachodu_01.JPG/330px-Widok_na_Perast_z_zachodu_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Widok_na_Perast_z_zachodu_01.JPG/440px-Widok_na_Perast_z_zachodu_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4457" data-file-height="3004"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Widok_na_Perast_z_zachodu_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Perast" title="Perast">Perast</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Kotor" title="Bay of Kotor">Bay of Kotor</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sveti_Stefan01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Sveti_Stefan01.JPG/220px-Sveti_Stefan01.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Sveti_Stefan01.JPG/330px-Sveti_Stefan01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Sveti_Stefan01.JPG/440px-Sveti_Stefan01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sveti_Stefan01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sveti_Stefan" title="Sveti Stefan">Sveti Stefan</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Montenegro has both a picturesque coast and a mountainous northern region. The country was a well-known tourist spot in the 1980s. Yet, the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugoslav wars">Yugoslav wars</a> that were fought in neighbouring countries during the 1990s crippled the tourist industry and damaged the image of Montenegro for years. </p>
      <p>With a total of 1.6&nbsp;million visitors, Montenegro is the 36th most visited country (out of 47 countries) in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> The Montenegrin <a href="/wiki/Adriatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Adriatic">Adriatic</a> coast is 295&nbsp;km (183&nbsp;mi) long, with 72&nbsp;km (45&nbsp;mi) of beaches and many well-preserved ancient old towns. <i><a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Traveler" title="National Geographic Traveler">National Geographic Traveler</a></i> (edited once a decade) ranks Montenegro among the "50 Places of a Lifetime", and the Montenegrin seaside <a href="/wiki/Sveti_Stefan" title="Sveti Stefan">Sveti Stefan</a> was used as the cover for the magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> The coast region of Montenegro is considered one of the great new "discoveries" among world tourists. In January 2010, <i>The New York Times</i> ranked the Ulcinj South Coast region of Montenegro, including <a href="/wiki/Velika_Plaza" class="mw-redirect" title="Velika Plaza">Velika Plaza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ada_Bojana" title="Ada Bojana">Ada Bojana</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Mediteran" title="Hotel Mediteran">Hotel Mediteran</a> of Ulcinj, among the "Top 31 Places to Go in 2010" as part of a worldwide ranking of tourism destinations.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Montenegro was also listed by Yahoo Travel among the "10 Top Hot Spots of 2009" to visit, describing it as being "[c]urrently ranked as the second fastest growing tourism market in the world (falling just behind China)".<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> It is listed every year by prestigious tourism guides like Lonely Planet as a top tourist destination along with Greece, Spain and other popular locations.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It was not until the 2000s that the tourism industry began to recover, and the country has since experienced a high rate of growth in the number of visits and overnight stays. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Montenegro" title="Demographics of Montenegro">Demographics of Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Montenegro" title="Demographic history of Montenegro">Demographic history of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_structure">Ethnic structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ethnic structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MontenegroEthnic2011.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/MontenegroEthnic2011.PNG/180px-MontenegroEthnic2011.PNG" decoding="async" width="180" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/MontenegroEthnic2011.PNG/270px-MontenegroEthnic2011.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/MontenegroEthnic2011.PNG/360px-MontenegroEthnic2011.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1911" data-file-height="2388"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MontenegroEthnic2011.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Predominant ethnic group in each municipality of Montenegro, 2011.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the 2003 census, Montenegro has 620,145 citizens. If the methodology used up to 1991 had been adopted in the 2003 census, Montenegro would officially have recorded 673,094 citizens. The results of the 2011 census show that Montenegro had 620,029 citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-census2011_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2011-85">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Montenegro is a <a href="/wiki/Multinational_state" title="Multinational state">multiethnic state</a> in which no ethnic group forms a majority.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> Major ethnic groups include <a href="/wiki/Montenegrins_(ethnic_group)" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegrins (ethnic group)">Montenegrins</a> (Црногорци/<i>Crnogorci</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a> (Срби/<i>Srbi</i>); others are <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a> (<i>Bošnjaci</i>), <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a> (<i>Albanci&nbsp;– Shqiptarët</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a> (<i>Hrvati</i>). The number of "Montenegrins" and "Serbs" fluctuates widely from census to census due to changes in how people perceive, experience, or choose to express, their identity and ethnic affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsible-leftside-toggle mw-collapsed" style="box-sizing:border-box;width:100%;font-size:95%;padding:4px;border:none;">
       <div style="font-size:100%;line-height:1.6;font-weight:bold;background:transparent;text-align:left;;">

       </div>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Montenegro" title="Languages of Montenegro">Languages of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MontenegroLanguage2011.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/MontenegroLanguage2011.PNG/180px-MontenegroLanguage2011.PNG" decoding="async" width="180" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/MontenegroLanguage2011.PNG/270px-MontenegroLanguage2011.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/MontenegroLanguage2011.PNG/360px-MontenegroLanguage2011.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1911" data-file-height="2388"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MontenegroLanguage2011.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Linguistic structure of Montenegro by settlements, 2011.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The official language in Montenegro is <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a>. Also, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a> are recognized in usage. Montenegrin, Serbian, Bosnian, and Croatian are <a href="/wiki/Mutually_intelligible" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutually intelligible">mutually intelligible</a>, all being <a href="/wiki/Standard_varieties" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard varieties">standard varieties</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Serbo-Croatian language">Serbo-Croatian language</a>. Montenegrin is the plurality mother-tongue of the population under 18 years of age.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> Previous constitutions endorsed Serbo-Croatian as the official language in <a href="/wiki/SR_Montenegro" class="mw-redirect" title="SR Montenegro">SR Montenegro</a> and Serbian of the <a href="/wiki/Ijekavian" class="mw-redirect" title="Ijekavian">Ijekavian</a> standard during the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Montenegro_(federal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Montenegro (federal)">1992–2006 period</a>. </p> 
      <div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsible-leftside-toggle mw-collapsed" style="box-sizing:border-box;width:100%;font-size:95%;padding:4px;border:none;">
       <div style="font-size:100%;line-height:1.6;font-weight:bold;background:transparent;text-align:left;;">
        Languages (2011 census)
       </div>
       <div class="mw-collapsible-content" style="background:transparent;text-align:left;;">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Montenegro" title="Religion in Montenegro">Religion in Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Monasterio_de_Ostrog,_Montenegro,_2014-04-14,_DD_14.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Monasterio_de_Ostrog%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-14%2C_DD_14.JPG/220px-Monasterio_de_Ostrog%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-14%2C_DD_14.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Monasterio_de_Ostrog%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-14%2C_DD_14.JPG/330px-Monasterio_de_Ostrog%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-14%2C_DD_14.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Monasterio_de_Ostrog%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-14%2C_DD_14.JPG/440px-Monasterio_de_Ostrog%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-14%2C_DD_14.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5395" data-file-height="3597"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Monasterio_de_Ostrog,_Montenegro,_2014-04-14,_DD_14.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ostrog_Monastery" title="Ostrog Monastery">Ostrog Monastery</a> is a well-known place of <a href="/wiki/Christian_pilgrimage" title="Christian pilgrimage">pilgrimage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Montenegro has been historically at the crossroads of multiculturalism and over centuries this has shaped its unique form of co-existence between Muslim and Christian populations.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> Montenegrins have been, historically, members of the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Orthodox Church</a> (governed by the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitanate_of_Montenegro_and_the_Littoral" title="Metropolitanate of Montenegro and the Littoral">Metropolitanate of Montenegro and the Littoral</a>), and Serbian Orthodox Christianity is the most popular religion today in Montenegro. The <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_Orthodox_Church" title="Montenegrin Orthodox Church">Montenegrin Orthodox Church</a> was recently founded and is followed by a small minority of Montenegrins although it is not in communion with any other Christian Orthodox Church as it has not been officially recognized. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Prcanj-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Prcanj-01.jpg/220px-Prcanj-01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Prcanj-01.jpg/330px-Prcanj-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Prcanj-01.jpg/440px-Prcanj-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Prcanj-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Our Lady's Temple of <a href="/wiki/Pr%C4%8Danj" title="Prčanj">Prčanj</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite tensions between religious groups during the <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">Bosnian War</a>, Montenegro remained fairly stable, mainly due its population having a historic perspective on religious tolerance and faith diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> Religious institutions from Montenegro all have guaranteed rights and are separate from the state. The second largest religion is Islam, which amounts to 19% of the total population of the country. A little more than one-fourth of <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a> are <a href="/wiki/Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> (8,126 in the 2004 census) while the other three-fourths (22,267) are mainly <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslims">Sunni Muslims</a>; in 2012 a protocol passed that recognizes <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> as an official religion in Montenegro, ensures that <a href="/wiki/Halal" title="Halal">halal</a> foods will be served at military facilities, hospitals, dormitories and all social facilities; and that Muslim women will be permitted to wear headscarves in schools and at public institutions, as well as ensuring that Muslims have the right to take Fridays off work for the <a href="/wiki/Jumu%27ah" title="Jumu'ah">Jumu'ah</a> (Friday)-prayer.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> Since the time of <a href="/wiki/Vojislavljevi%C4%87_dynasty" title="Vojislavljević dynasty">Vojislavljević dynasty</a> Catholicism is autochthonous in Montenegrin area.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> There is also a small Roman Catholic population, mostly Albanians with some Croats, divided between the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Bar" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Bar">Archdiocese of Antivari</a> headed by the Primate of Serbia and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Kotor" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Kotor">Diocese of Kotor</a> that is a part of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Croatia" title="Catholic Church in Croatia">Catholic Church in Croatia</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_-_Mosque_-_Flickr_-_raymond_zoller.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/%D0%9C%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_-_Mosque_-_Flickr_-_raymond_zoller.jpg/220px-%D0%9C%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_-_Mosque_-_Flickr_-_raymond_zoller.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/%D0%9C%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_-_Mosque_-_Flickr_-_raymond_zoller.jpg/330px-%D0%9C%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_-_Mosque_-_Flickr_-_raymond_zoller.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/%D0%9C%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_-_Mosque_-_Flickr_-_raymond_zoller.jpg/440px-%D0%9C%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_-_Mosque_-_Flickr_-_raymond_zoller.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4862" data-file-height="3241"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%8C_-_Mosque_-_Flickr_-_raymond_zoller.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Selimia Mosque in <a href="/wiki/Bar,_Montenegro" title="Bar, Montenegro">Bar</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Religious determination according to the 2011 census:<sup id="cite_ref-census2011_85-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2011-85">[84]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Montenegro" title="Education in Montenegro">Education in Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cetinje,_Montenegro_-_panoramio_(15).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Cetinje%2C_Montenegro_-_panoramio_%2815%29.jpg/220px-Cetinje%2C_Montenegro_-_panoramio_%2815%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Cetinje%2C_Montenegro_-_panoramio_%2815%29.jpg/330px-Cetinje%2C_Montenegro_-_panoramio_%2815%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Cetinje%2C_Montenegro_-_panoramio_%2815%29.jpg/440px-Cetinje%2C_Montenegro_-_panoramio_%2815%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="3216"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cetinje,_Montenegro_-_panoramio_(15).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Montenegro" title="National Library of Montenegro">National Library of Montenegro</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cetinje" title="Cetinje">Cetinje</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education in Montenegro is regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Montenegro" title="Government of Montenegro">Montenegrin Ministry of Education and Science</a>. </p>
      <p>Education starts in either pre-schools or elementary schools. Children enroll in elementary schools (<a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a>: <i>Osnovna škola</i>) at the age of 6; it lasts 9 years. The students may continue their secondary education (<a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a>: <i>Srednja škola</i>), which lasts 4 years (3 years for trade schools) and ends with graduation (<a href="/wiki/Matura" title="Matura">Matura</a>). Higher education lasts with a certain first degree after 3 to 6 years. There is one public university (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Montenegro" title="University of Montenegro">University of Montenegro</a>) and two private ones (<a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_University" title="Mediterranean University">Mediterranean University</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Donja_Gorica" title="University of Donja Gorica">University of Donja Gorica</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elementary_and_secondary_education">Elementary and secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Elementary and secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Elementary education in Montenegro is free and compulsory for all the children between the ages of 7 and 15 when children attend the "eight-year school". </p>
      <p>Various types of elementary education are available to all who qualify, but the vocational and technical schools (gymnasiums), where the students follow four-year course which will take them up to the university entrance, are the most popular. At the secondary level there are a number of art schools, apprentice schools and teacher training schools. Those who have attended the technical schools may pursue their education further at one of two-year post-secondary schools, created in response to the needs of industry and the social services. </p>
      <p>Secondary schools are divided in three types, and children attend one depending on choice and primary school grades: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">Gymnasium</a> (Gimnazija / Гимназиjа) lasts for four years and offers a general, broad education. It is a preparatory school for university, and hence the most academic and prestigious.</li> 
       <li>Professional schools (Stručna škola / Стручна школа) last for three or four years and specialize students in certain fields which may result in their attending college; professional schools offer a relatively broad education.</li> 
       <li>Vocational schools (Zanatska škola / Занатска школа) last for three years and focus on vocational education (e.g., joinery, plumbing, mechanics) without an option of continuing education after three years.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary_education">Tertiary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Tertiary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Tertiary level institutions are divided into "Higher education" (Više obrazovanje) and "High education" (Visoko obrazovanje) level faculties. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Colleges (Fakultet) and art academies (akademija umjetnosti) last between 4 and 6 years (one year is two semesters long) and award diplomas equivalent to a Bachelor of Arts or a Bachelor of Science degree.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Higher schools (Viša škola) lasts between two and four years. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-graduate_education">Post-graduate education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Post-graduate education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Post-graduate education (post-diplomske studije) is offered after tertiary level and offers <a href="/wiki/Masters%27_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="Masters' degree">Masters' degrees</a>, PhD and specialization education. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Montenegro" title="Culture of Montenegro">Culture of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vladin_Dom_(Dom_Rz%C4%85dowy)_w_Cetinje_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Vladin_Dom_%28Dom_Rz%C4%85dowy%29_w_Cetinje_01.jpg/220px-Vladin_Dom_%28Dom_Rz%C4%85dowy%29_w_Cetinje_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Vladin_Dom_%28Dom_Rz%C4%85dowy%29_w_Cetinje_01.jpg/330px-Vladin_Dom_%28Dom_Rz%C4%85dowy%29_w_Cetinje_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Vladin_Dom_%28Dom_Rz%C4%85dowy%29_w_Cetinje_01.jpg/440px-Vladin_Dom_%28Dom_Rz%C4%85dowy%29_w_Cetinje_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3185" data-file-height="2123"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vladin_Dom_(Dom_Rz%C4%85dowy)_w_Cetinje_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Montenegro" title="National Museum of Montenegro">National Museum of Montenegro</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The culture of Montenegro has been shaped by a variety of influences throughout history. The influence of Orthodox, Ottoman (Turk), Slavic, Central European, and seafaring Adriatic cultures (notably parts of Italy, like the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Republic of Venice</a>) have been the most important in recent centuries. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Museo_Mar%C3%ADtimo,_Kotor,_Bah%C3%ADa_de_Kotor,_Montenegro,_2014-04-19,_DD_31.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Museo_Mar%C3%ADtimo%2C_Kotor%2C_Bah%C3%ADa_de_Kotor%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-19%2C_DD_31.JPG/220px-Museo_Mar%C3%ADtimo%2C_Kotor%2C_Bah%C3%ADa_de_Kotor%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-19%2C_DD_31.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Museo_Mar%C3%ADtimo%2C_Kotor%2C_Bah%C3%ADa_de_Kotor%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-19%2C_DD_31.JPG/330px-Museo_Mar%C3%ADtimo%2C_Kotor%2C_Bah%C3%ADa_de_Kotor%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-19%2C_DD_31.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Museo_Mar%C3%ADtimo%2C_Kotor%2C_Bah%C3%ADa_de_Kotor%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-19%2C_DD_31.JPG/440px-Museo_Mar%C3%ADtimo%2C_Kotor%2C_Bah%C3%ADa_de_Kotor%2C_Montenegro%2C_2014-04-19%2C_DD_31.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3511" data-file-height="2636"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Museo_Mar%C3%ADtimo,_Kotor,_Bah%C3%ADa_de_Kotor,_Montenegro,_2014-04-19,_DD_31.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Maritime Museum in <a href="/wiki/Kotor" title="Kotor">Kotor</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Montenegro has many significant cultural and historical sites, including heritage sites from the pre-<a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gothic_art" title="Gothic art">Gothic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> periods. The Montenegrin coastal region is especially well known for its religious monuments, including the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Saint_Tryphon" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of Saint Tryphon">Cathedral of Saint Tryphon</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kotor" title="Kotor">Kotor</a><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> (Cattaro under the Venetians), the basilica of St. Luke (over 800 years), <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_the_Rocks" title="Our Lady of the Rocks">Our Lady of the Rocks</a> (Škrpjela), the <a href="/wiki/Savina_monastery_(Montenegro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Savina monastery (Montenegro)">Savina Monastery</a> and others. Medieval monasteries contain a number of artistically important frescoes. </p>
      <p>A dimension of Montenegrin culture is the ethical ideal of <i>Čojstvo i Junaštvo</i>, "Humaneness and Gallantry".<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> The traditional folk dance of the Montenegrins is the <a href="/wiki/Oro_(eagle_dance)" title="Oro (eagle dance)">Oro</a>, the "eagle dance" that involves dancing in circles with couples alternating in the centre, and is finished by forming a human pyramid by dancers standing on each other's shoulders. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Carnival_in_Tivat_2019_(Montenegro)_11.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Carnival_in_Tivat_2019_%28Montenegro%29_11.jpg/220px-Carnival_in_Tivat_2019_%28Montenegro%29_11.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Carnival_in_Tivat_2019_%28Montenegro%29_11.jpg/330px-Carnival_in_Tivat_2019_%28Montenegro%29_11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Carnival_in_Tivat_2019_%28Montenegro%29_11.jpg/440px-Carnival_in_Tivat_2019_%28Montenegro%29_11.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7360" data-file-height="4912"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Carnival_in_Tivat_2019_(Montenegro)_11.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Carnival in Tivat 2019.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Montenegro's capital, Podgorica, and the former royal capital of Cetinje are the two most important centres of culture and the arts in the country. </p>
      <p>The American author <a href="/wiki/Rex_Stout" title="Rex Stout">Rex Stout</a> wrote a long series of detective novels featuring his fictional creation <a href="/wiki/Nero_Wolfe" title="Nero Wolfe">Nero Wolfe</a>, who was born in Montenegro. His Nero Wolfe novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Black_Mountain_(novel)" title="The Black Mountain (novel)">The Black Mountain</a></i> was largely set in Montenegro during the 1950s. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Montenegro" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Montenegro">Media of Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The media of Montenegro refers to mass media outlets based in Montenegro. Television, magazines, and newspapers are all operated by both state-owned and for-profit corporations which depend on advertising, <a href="/wiki/Subscription" class="mw-redirect" title="Subscription">subscription</a>, and other sales-related revenues. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Montenegro" title="Constitution of Montenegro">Constitution of Montenegro</a> guarantees freedom of speech. As a <a href="/wiki/Country_in_transition" class="mw-redirect" title="Country in transition">country in transition</a>, Montenegro's media system is under transformation. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_cuisine" title="Montenegrin cuisine">Montenegrin cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Foods_from_Montenegro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Foods_from_Montenegro.jpg/220px-Foods_from_Montenegro.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Foods_from_Montenegro.jpg/330px-Foods_from_Montenegro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Foods_from_Montenegro.jpg/440px-Foods_from_Montenegro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="626" data-file-height="389"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Foods_from_Montenegro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Foods from Montenegro
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Montenegrin cuisine is a result of Montenegro's long history. It is a variation of Mediterranean and Oriental. The most influence is from Italy, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>/<a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, and Hungary. Montenegrin cuisine also varies geographically; the cuisine in the coastal area differs from the one in the northern highland region. The coastal area is traditionally a representative of <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_cuisine" title="Mediterranean cuisine">Mediterranean cuisine</a>, with seafood being a common dish, while the northern represents more the Oriental. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Montenegro" title="Sport in Montenegro">Sport in Montenegro</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nikola_Vucevic_Dec_2013_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nikola_Vucevic_Dec_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Nikola_Vucevic_Dec_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nikola_Vucevic_Dec_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Nikola_Vucevic_Dec_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nikola_Vucevic_Dec_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Nikola_Vucevic_Dec_2013_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2936" data-file-height="2891"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nikola_Vucevic_Dec_2013_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Nikola_Vu%C4%8Devi%C4%87" title="Nikola Vučević">Nikola Vučević</a>, a professional <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> player for the <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Magic" title="Orlando Magic">Orlando Magic</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> (<a href="/wiki/NBA" class="mw-redirect" title="NBA">NBA</a>).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <b>Sports in Montenegro</b> revolves mostly around <a href="/wiki/Team_sport" title="Team sport">team sports</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>. Other sports involved are <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">karate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Table_tennis" title="Table tennis">table tennis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">Water polo</a> is the most popular sport in Montenegro, and is considered the <a href="/wiki/National_sport" title="National sport">national sport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Popular_Sports_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Popular_Sports-100">[99]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Montenegro_men%27s_national_water_polo_team" title="Montenegro men's national water polo team">Montenegro men's national water polo team</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/FINA_Water_Polo_World_Rankings" title="FINA Water Polo World Rankings">top ranked</a> teams in the world, winning the gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Men%27s_European_Water_Polo_Championship" title="2008 Men's European Water Polo Championship">2008 Men's European Water Polo Championship</a> in <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="Málaga">Málaga</a>, Spain, and winning the gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/2009_FINA_Men%27s_Water_Polo_World_League" title="2009 FINA Men's Water Polo World League">2009 FINA Men's Water Polo World League</a>, which was held in the Montenegrin capital, <a href="/wiki/Podgorica" title="Podgorica">Podgorica</a>. The Montenegrin team <a href="/wiki/PVK_Primorac" class="mw-redirect" title="PVK Primorac">PVK Primorac</a> from <a href="/wiki/Kotor" title="Kotor">Kotor</a> became a champion of Europe at the <a href="/wiki/LEN_Euroleague" class="mw-redirect" title="LEN Euroleague">LEN Euroleague</a> 2009 in <a href="/wiki/Rijeka" title="Rijeka">Rijeka</a>, Croatia. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the second most popular sport in Montenegro.<sup id="cite_ref-Popular_Sports_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Popular_Sports-100">[99]</a></sup> Notable football players from Montenegro are <a href="/wiki/Dejan_Savi%C4%87evi%C4%87" title="Dejan Savićević">Dejan Savićević</a>, <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Mijatovi%C4%87" title="Predrag Mijatović">Predrag Mijatović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mirko_Vu%C4%8Dini%C4%87" title="Mirko Vučinić">Mirko Vučinić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Savi%C4%87" title="Stefan Savić">Stefan Savić</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stevan_Joveti%C4%87" title="Stevan Jovetić">Stevan Jovetić</a>. <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegrin national football team">Montenegrin national football team</a>, founded in 2006, played in playoffs for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a>, which is the biggest success in the history of the national team. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Montenegro_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegro national basketball team">Montenegro national basketball team</a> is also known for good performances and had won a lot of medals in the past as part of the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_basketball_team" title="Yugoslavia national basketball team">Yugoslavia national basketball team</a>. In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Federation_of_Montenegro" title="Basketball Federation of Montenegro">Basketball Federation of Montenegro</a> along with this team joined the <a href="/wiki/International_Basketball_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="International Basketball Federation">International Basketball Federation</a> (FIBA) on its own, following the <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_independence_referendum,_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Montenegrin independence referendum, 2006">Independence of Montenegro</a>. Montenegro participated on two Eurobaskets until now. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MontenegrinFans2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/MontenegrinFans2.jpg/220px-MontenegrinFans2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/MontenegrinFans2.jpg/330px-MontenegrinFans2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/MontenegrinFans2.jpg/440px-MontenegrinFans2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="408"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MontenegrinFans2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Podgorica_City_Stadium" title="Podgorica City Stadium">Podgorica City Stadium</a>, Montenegro fans with national features.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Among women sports, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro_women%27s_national_handball_team" title="Montenegro women's national handball team">the national handball team</a> is the most successful, having won the <a href="/wiki/2012_European_Women%27s_Handball_Championship" title="2012 European Women's Handball Championship">2012 European Championship</a> and finishing as runners-up at the <a href="/wiki/Handball_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Handball at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>. <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDRK_Budu%C4%87nost_Podgorica" title="ŽRK Budućnost Podgorica">ŽRK Budućnost Podgorica</a> won two times EHF Champions League. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">Chess</a> is another popular sport and some famous global chess players, like <a href="/wiki/Slavko_Dedi%C4%87" title="Slavko Dedić">Slavko Dedić</a>, were born in Montenegro. </p>
      <p>At the <a href="/wiki/Handball_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Handball at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Olympic Games</a> in London, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro_women%27s_national_handball_team" title="Montenegro women's national handball team">Montenegro women's national handball team</a> won the country's first Olympic medal by winning silver. They lost in the final to defending World, Olympic and European Champions, <a href="/wiki/Norway_women%27s_national_handball_team" title="Norway women's national handball team">Norway</a> 26–23. Following this defeat the team won against Norway in the final of the <a href="/wiki/2012_European_Women%27s_Handball_Championship" title="2012 European Women's Handball Championship">2012 European Championship</a>, becoming champions for the first time. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays">Public holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Public holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Montenegro_real_estate_taxes" title="Montenegro real estate taxes">Montenegro real estate taxes</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Montenegro" title="Outline of Montenegro">Outline of Montenegro</a></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montenegro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-status-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-status_56-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> Kosovo is the subject of a territorial dispute between the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Republic of Kosovo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Republic of Serbia</a>. The Republic of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> on 17 February 2008. <a href="/wiki/Kosovo%E2%80%93Serbia_relations" title="Kosovo–Serbia relations">Serbia continues to claim</a> it as part of its <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">own sovereign territory</a>. The two governments <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade–Pristina negotiations">began to normalise relations</a> in 2013, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">2013 Brussels Agreement</a>. Kosovo is currently recognized as an independent state by <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">98</a> out of the 193 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">United Nations member states</a>. In total, <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">113</a> UN member states recognized Kosovo at some point, of which <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">15</a> later withdrew their recognition.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
